FellowshipoftheRing is a fantasy novel by English author J. R. R. Tolkien. It is the first volume in his The Lord of the Rings trilogy, and was originally published in three volumes, from September 1954 to September 1955. The book is the story of a group of friends who set out on a quest to destroy a ring of power that was forged by the Dark Lord Sauron. The story is set in a fictional universe called Middle-earth. Fellowship of the Ring was the first book to win the British Academy Children's Book Award in 1956. The Fellowship of the Ring is a fantasy novel by English author J. R. R. Tolkien. It is the first volume in his The Lord of the Rings trilogy, and was originally published in three volumes, from September 1954 to September 1955. Karlsruhe is a city in the German state of Baden-Württemberg. It is located near the border with France in the foothills of the Black Forest, on the Rhine River. It is the administrative seat of the district of Karlsruhe. The city has a population of 228,889. Israel is a country in the Middle East. It is located on the eastern shore of the Mediterranean Sea. It is bordered by Lebanon to the north, Syria to the northeast, Jordan to the east, the Palestinian territories to the southeast, Egypt to the southwest, the Red Sea to the west, and the Gulf of Aqaba to the northwest. The country is noted for its beaches, desert landscapes, ancient ruins, and modern cities. It is also the site of Jerusalem, which is considered sacred by Jews, Christians, and Muslims. Modern Hebrew is a language spoken in Israel and by Israeli Jews worldwide. It is the official language of Israel and the official language of the State of Israel. It is one of the official languages of the Palestinian territories. It is also spoken in the United States, Canada, and Argentina by Israeli Jews. Banking Corporation of the Philippines (BCP) is the largest bank in the Philippines. It has 1,270 branches and 1,451 ATMs all over the Philippines. BCP has a presence in Hong Kong, China, Singapore, and the United States. The bank was formed by the merger of Bank of the Philippine Islands (BPI) and Chinabank on June 7, 1998.

Dwejra, għall-Kbir Ħamrun, is a small town in the southeast of Malta. It is situated on the south-eastern tip of Malta, next to the town of Żebbuġ. It is a small town with a population of around 5,000. It is one of the three local councils that make up the Southern Region of Malta.  The town is one of the most popular tourist destinations in Malta and attracts visitors from all over the world, as it has the only natural harbour in Malta, which is sheltered by a natural breakwater, formed by the islands of Filfla and the Three Cities. The town is also famous for the Blue Lagoon, a small natural harbour, which is situated just off the coast of Dwejra. Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born April 27, 1937 in Saint Petersburg, Russia) is a Russian mathematician. She is known for her contributions to algebraic geometry, including the Bondarev–Shapley theorem, a classification of surfaces in three-dimensional space, and the resolution of the Tarski problem.

Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born 30 August 1934 in Leningrad, Russia) is a mathematician who made important contributions to mathematical physics and to algebraic geometry. She was awarded the Fields Medal in 1966 "for her contributions to algebraic geometry and its applications in mathematical physics". In 1966, she and her husband, Dmitri I. Shapiro, proved the so-called Bondarev–Shapiro theorem, which is a fundamental theorem of algebraic geometry. In 1973, she proved the existence of K3 surfaces with any given number of isolated rational double points. She is a professor at the Steklov Institute of Mathematics in Moscow. Bondareva is the author of over 200 publications. Bondareva is married to Dmitri I. Shapiro.  She was awarded the Fields Medal in 1966.  Bondareva is the author of over 200 publications.  She is a professor at the Steklov Institute of Mathematics in Moscow.

Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born April 27, 1937 in Leningrad) is a Russian mathematician who made important contributions to mathematical physics, in particular to celestial mechanics. She is best known for her contribution to the proof of the stability of the solar system. She was the first woman to become a full professor of mathematics at a Russian university.

Banking in China The Chinabank is a large commercial bank in the Philippines. It has more than 2,000 branches and 3,000 ATMs in the country. It was founded in May 1993. The Chinabank is a major shareholder of the Chinabank Commercial Banking Corporation, which is a wholly-owned subsidiary. It has an extensive network in China, including branches in Hong Kong, Taiwan, Macau, and Shanghai. It also has a branch in the Philippines. The Chinabank has a total of $33.3 billion in assets.

Bedford Aerodrome, għall-Kbir Ħamrun, is a former civil airport in Malta. It was located in Ħamrun, Malta. It was closed in 2008 after the opening of the new MIA airport in Luqa. MotorSport Vision is a motorsport organisation based in Malta. It was founded by Peter Ogden in 2004.  Peter Ogden was born in Cardiff, Wales, in 1977. He moved to Malta with his family in 1988. He took up karting in 1994 and joined the MotorSport Vision team in 2003.

Darinka Dentcheva (en maltés Darinka Dentiċeva) és una matemàtica especialitzada en optimització matemàtica i anàlisi estocàstica. És professora a la Universitat de Califòrnia a Berkeley. També és una de les autores del llibre de text Introduction to Mathematical Programming.  Dentcheva va néixer a Ialoveni, República Socialista Soviètica de Bulgària, actualment a Moldàvia. Va estudiar a la Universitat de Sofia i a la Universitat Estatal de Moscou, on es va doctorar el 1983. Va fer de professora a la Universitat de Sofia, a la Universitat Estatal de Moscou i a la Universitat de Califòrnia a Berkeley.  El seu treball es centra en la programació matemàtica i la programació estocàstica. Va obtenir el premi George B. Dantzig el 1991. És membre de l'Acadèmia Nacional de Ciències dels Estats Units, de l'Acadèmia Europea de Ciències i Arts i de l'Acadèmia Americana d'Arts i Ciències. Liselotte Grschebina is a German-born Israeli singer. She was born in Karlsruhe, Germany, and immigrated to Israel with her family in 1961. She was married to the Israeli musician David Tishman and had two children, daughter Inbal Tishman and son Yonatan Tishman.  Liselotte Grschebina died on 14 June 1994 in Jerusalem, Israel, of a heart attack.  Liselotte Grschebina is known for her hit singles "Beautiful", "Now or Never", and "Wait". Her other songs include "When the Night Comes", "Just the Way I Am", and "Don't Cry".  She was awarded the Israel Prize in 1999. Her albums include The Singer and In Love Again. Liselotte Grschebina is a German-born Israeli singer. She was born in Karlsruhe, Germany, on May 2, 1908, and died in Tel Aviv on June 14, 1994. She had a long career as a singer, and was the first woman to record music in Hebrew. In the 1950s she was also a television host, known as "the first lady of television in Israel".  Grschebina was born in Karlsruhe, Germany. In the early 1930s, she moved to Paris to study singing, and in 1936 she moved to Palestine. In the 1930s and 1940s, she was a member of the Palestine Radio Orchestra. She also sang with the Palestine Symphony Orchestra. In the 1950s, she was the host of the popular television show Kol Yisrael ("All of Israel").  She was married to the conductor and composer Shmuel Ashkenazi. Her son, David Ashkenazi, is a composer. In 1994, she was awarded the Israel Prize for Music.

Acharya Institute of Technology is an Autonomous Institution under the Visvesvaraya Technological University. It is a co-educational institute and was established in 2004. The institute offers undergraduate, postgraduate and doctoral courses in engineering and technology. The institute is located in the heart of Bangalore, the Silicon Valley of India, and is spread over an area of 120 acres. The institute has a state-of-the-art infrastructure with facilities for various sports and recreation activities.

Acharya Institute of Technology is an Autonomous Institution under Visvesvaraya Technological University. It is located at the heart of the city of Bangalore in Karnataka. The institute has been established to meet the increasing demand for technical education in the country. The institute is affiliated to the Visvesvaraya Technological University, Belgaum, Karnataka, India. Brandon Carter, il est un physicien britannique, né le 25 février 1949 à Londres. Il est spécialiste de la relativité générale et de la cosmologie. Il est notamment connu pour son travail sur le théorème du trou noir de la relativité générale. En 2007, il a reçu le prix Shaw en mathématiques pour ses contributions à la relativité générale, en particulier pour son travail sur la constante cosmologique de l'équation d'état de l'énergie noire. Il a travaillé à l'université de Princeton, à l'université de Californie à Santa Barbara, à l'université de Princeton, à l'université de Californie à Los Angeles, à l'université de Cambridge, à l'Institut Perimeter de physique théorique, et à l'université de Cambridge. Il est membre de la Royal Society. Il est professeur à l'université de Cambridge depuis 2003. Il est connu pour avoir introduit le concept d'énergie sombre et la constante cosmologique dans le cadre de la relativité générale. Il a développé la théorie de l'état de l'art, la théorie des trous noirs et la théorie de la relativité générale, ainsi que les équations de champ de la relativité générale et la théorie de la gravitation de Kaluza-Klein. En plus de son travail sur la relativité générale, il a travaillé sur la théorie des champs unifiés, les cordes et la gravité quantique. Il a également travaillé sur la théorie des champs quantiques et la théorie des champs scalaires. Il a également travaillé sur les théories des champs classiques et sur les champs quantiques. Il a également travaillé sur la théorie des champs unifiés, les cordes et la gravité quantique. Il a également travaillé sur la théorie des champs quantiques et la théorie des champs scalaires. Il a également travaillé sur les théories des champs classiques et sur les champs quantiques. Il a également travaillé sur la théorie des champs unifiés, les cordes et la gravité quantique. Il a également travaillé sur la théorie des champs quantiques et la théorie des champs scalaires. Il a également travaillé sur les théories des champs classiques et sur les champs quantiques. The Velvet Underground & Nico is an American rock band formed in 1964 in New York City. The band was led by singer and guitarist Lou Reed, who wrote most of the songs with his bandmates John Cale, Sterling Morrison, and Maureen Tucker, and is the only original member to have remained in the band throughout its entire existence. The band was initially known for its minimalist and idiosyncratic style, and for Reed's experimental songwriting. The Velvet Underground were an important influence on the development of punk rock, and their music has been the subject of a large body of critical analysis. They are often cited as one of the most influential bands of the 1960s, and have been referred to as one of the most important bands in rock and roll history. In February 2014, Rolling Stone ranked the Velvet Underground at number 35 on their list of the 100 Greatest Artists of All Time.

Dwejra, għall-Ingliżjoni, is a small town in the southeast of Malta. It is situated on the south-eastern tip of the island of Malta. It is surrounded by a lagoon and is the only inhabited settlement on the east coast. The town is also known for the Blue Lagoon, a popular tourist attraction.  The town was founded in the 9th century, when it was named Birgu, and was part of the Order of Saint John, which ruled Malta from 1530 to 1798. The Order's headquarters were located in the town. The town is also known as the birthplace of the Maltese national anthem, 'Għana tal-Malti'.  Dwejra was also known as the main port of Malta, as the Grand Harbour is the largest natural harbour in the Mediterranean. The main entrance to the harbour is the Marsamxett Harbour, which is situated in the town. Dwejra is also the location of the Azure Window, a natural arch in the rocky cliffs of the coastline.  The town has a population of 4,076, and has a total area of 4.9 km². The town is divided into two districts, namely Dwejra and Għall-Ingliżjoni.  The town is served by Dwejra railway station, which is the terminus of the main railway line on the island. It is also served by the Dwejra bus station, which is the terminus of the main bus routes in Malta.  Dwejra is also home to the Dwejra Power Station, which is the largest power station in Malta. The power station was opened in 1970, and has a capacity of 300 MW. It was built to provide electricity to the island's southern region. It is also home to the largest desalination plant in Malta, which was opened in 2001. The desalination plant was built to provide water to the southern region of the island. It has a capacity of 60,000 m³ of water per day.  Dwejra is a popular tourist attraction. The Blue Lagoon is a popular tourist attraction. The Blue Lagoon is a large sea cave, which is located on the eastern side of the town. The Blue Lagoon is surrounded by a lagoon, and is home to many marine species. Liselotte Grschebina is a German-Jewish poet, writer and journalist. She was born in Karlsruhe in 1908 and died in Israel in 1992. She was born to a family of Russian-Jewish origin. She spent most of her childhood in the Russian Empire. In 1922 she returned to Germany, where she studied at the University of Freiburg. After her marriage to the physicist Otto Grschebina, she moved to Palestine in 1936. In the 1930s and 1940s she worked as a journalist for the newspaper Der Jude. In the 1950s and 1960s she worked as a writer, translator and editor for the Israeli press. In 1979 she received the Israel Prize for her poetry.  Her poetry is considered part of the German-Jewish literary tradition. Her works are characterized by a strong Jewish feeling and a specific style, influenced by the German expressionism. Her poetry is characterized by a special rhythm and a metrical quality. The rhythm of her poems is based on the repetition of certain words or phrases. Grschebina's poems are considered a continuation of the Jewish poetry of the nineteenth century, influenced by the poetry of the German-Jewish poet Franz Rosenzweig. Her poems are often described as a poetic form of prayer.

E-Vinyl, the label that brought you the excellent No Light, is happy to announce the release of the Year of No Light album by Nord. The album, which was recorded in Oslo, Norway in 2009, will be released on May 1, 2010. The album features three new songs and two live versions of songs from the previous Nord album, Traces of Time.  The band, Nord, is a trio consisting of guitarist and vocalist Stian Carstensen, drummer Eivind Opsvik and bass player Kristian Sætre. The band has been together since 2007, and their debut album, Traces of Time, was released in 2008. The band is now back with their second album, Year of No Light.  Nord has been touring in Norway, Sweden, Denmark and Germany. Their music is described as a mix of folk, pop and electronica, and they have been called Norway’s answer to The Beatles.  The album will be available in both CD and vinyl format, and will also be available digitally. The album can be pre-ordered at www.e-vinyl.no  The band will be touring in Norway and Sweden in May 2010, and are also looking for a tour in the UK. For more information, visit www.nord.no. Darinka Dentcheva is an optimization researcher with a background in mathematics. Her professional interests include stochastic programming, combinatorial optimization and mathematical modelling of real-world problems. She has worked on a variety of topics, ranging from resource allocation to the management of health care systems. Her research is motivated by the desire to find practical, efficient and fair solutions to problems in different areas, including the management of natural resources and the provision of public services. Dr. Dentcheva has published over 80 research papers in the field of optimization. She has been the recipient of a number of awards and distinctions, including the first prize of the European Operations Research Society (EURO) in 2002, and the Friedrich Wilhelm Bessel Research Award of the Alexander von Humboldt Foundation in 2005. Dr. Dentcheva is a full professor at Humboldt University of Berlin. She is also an assistant professor at the University of Warwick in the United Kingdom. She is a fellow of the EURO and of the Royal Society of Arts. She is also an associate editor of the EURO Journal on Computational Economics. Dr. Dentcheva is a member of the Executive Committee of the International Federation of Operational Research Societies (IFORS).

Acharya Institute of Technology (AIT) is a constituent college of Visvesvaraya Technological University (VTU) located in Bangalore, Karnataka, India. The institute was established in 2000. It offers courses in engineering, technology and management. The institute is located in the heart of Bangalore, the Silicon Valley of India, and is easily accessible by all means of transportation. The college has a dedicated team of faculty members who are committed to imparting quality education to the students. The institute has been rated as one of the best engineering colleges in India by the National Institutional Ranking Framework (NIRF) of the Ministry of Human Resource Development (MHRD). The college offers a wide range of undergraduate and postgraduate programmes in engineering, technology and management. The college has a dedicated team of faculty members who are committed to imparting quality education to the students. The institute has been rated as one of the best engineering colleges in India by the National Institutional Ranking Framework (NIRF) of the Ministry of Human Resource Development (MHRD).

L-Ana-Mo'nson, Lady Anne Monson (b. Darlington, d. London, 27 Dec. 1753), was an English writer. She is best remembered for her popular memoirs, in which she described the lives of people in her circle, and for her travel accounts. She also wrote a novel, The Virgin Unmasked (1761), which was based on her own experiences, and was the first novel to have a heroine with a non-heteronormative sexuality. Monson was a friend of Mary Wollstonecraft and was the first Englishwoman to travel to the United States.  Monson was born in 1714 at Darlington Hall, in the north of England. She was the daughter of John Monson, a wealthy merchant, and his wife, Mary, the daughter of Sir John Clotworthy, 1st Baronet, of Dunston Hall. In 1720, her father became a member of parliament, and the family moved to London. Her mother died in 1721, and Monson was left in the care of her father's second wife, a widow with whom he had three daughters. She had little formal education, but was well read, and became a friend of the writer Mary Delany. At the age of sixteen, Monson was given a small income, and she began to write poetry and travel books.  In 1738, she published A Voyage from London to Paris, describing her journey from London to Paris, with an account of the sights of the two cities. In 1739, she published Letters from Paris, a collection of letters about her travels in France. In 1741, she published Letters from Italy, describing her travels in Italy. In 1745, she published Letters from Madrid and Lisbon, describing her travels in Spain and Portugal. In 1746, she published Letters from Paris and Italy, a collection of letters about her travels in France and Italy. In 1747, she published Letters from Spain and Portugal, a collection of letters about her travels in Spain and Portugal. In 1751, she published Letters from Italy, France, and Spain, a collection of letters about her travels in Italy, France, and Spain. In 1753, she published Letters from France, a collection of letters about her travels in France.  She married John Townshend, 2nd Viscount Townshend, in 1738, but the marriage was childless. L-Ana-Mo'nson, Lady Anne Monson (1726-1776), was the eldest daughter of George Monson, 3rd Earl of Farnham, and his wife, Mary Cary. She was born at Darlington, County Durham, England. She was the sister of Mary Monson, who was also born at Darlington. She was educated at home by her father and by Lady Mary Cary. She married the Hon. John Coventry, son of the Earl of Coventry, in 1745. She died at Baramahal, India, on 18 February 1776, and was buried at St. George's Church, Calcutta. She was the mother of John Coventry, 1st Earl of Coventry, who was born in India.

Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born 9 December 1951 in Leningrad, USSR) is a Russian economist and mathematician. She is a professor of economics at the Moscow State Institute of International Relations (MGIMO). She is also a member of the Russian Academy of Sciences. Bondareva is known for her contributions to game theory, especially in the area of bargaining and voting theory.  Bondareva was born in Leningrad, USSR. She graduated from the Department of Mathematics at the Leningrad State University in 1975, and obtained her PhD from the same university in 1983. She worked as a researcher at the Institute of Cybernetics at the Leningrad Academy of Sciences from 1975 to 1985, and was a professor at the Moscow State Institute of International Relations from 1985 to 1998. From 1998 to 2002 she was a professor at the Moscow State University. She is currently a professor at MGIMO. She is also a member of the Russian Academy of Sciences.  Bondareva is known for her contributions to game theory, especially in the area of bargaining and voting theory. She is known for her work on cooperative game theory, particularly in the area of non-cooperative bargaining theory. Her work on bargaining theory has been recognized as a contribution to the theory of bargaining by the Nobel laureate Thomas Schelling. Bondareva is also known for her work on voting theory and social choice theory. She has also made contributions to the theory of the firm.  She is the author of over 160 scientific publications, including over 40 articles in international scientific journals and monographs. She has supervised over 20 PhD theses and has participated in over 30 international scientific conferences. She is a member of the editorial board of the international scientific journal "Journal of Economic Theory" and of the Russian scientific journal "Optimization and Economics".  Bondareva was awarded the State Prize of the Russian Federation in 2005. She was elected as a member of the Russian Academy of Sciences in 2003. She was elected as a Fellow of the Econometric Society in 2000, and became a member of the International Academy of the Mathematical Sciences in 2009. She is a member of the International Association for Game Theory, and a member of the European Association for Evolutionary Political Economy.  Bondareva is married to the economist and mathematician Alexei Ryzhik. She is the mother of the mathematician and economist Olga Ryzh

Brandon Carter, is a professional physicist and astrophysicist, who is known for his work on general relativity. He is a professor of physics at the California Institute of Technology (Caltech) in Pasadena, California. Carter's most famous work is the Carter constant, which is used to study black holes, and the no-hair theorem, which states that black holes are completely described by only three physical parameters. He is also known for his work on the Carter-Penrose diagram, which is a graphical representation of the Kerr metric, which is a solution to Einstein's equations. Carter is the author of the book Gravitation (1972) with Robert Scheckner. Carter earned his PhD in physics from the University of Cambridge, England in 1963. Carter is a Fellow of the Royal Society and a member of the National Academy of Sciences. He is a member of the Pontifical Academy of Sciences. He is also a fellow of the American Academy of Arts and Sciences.

Darinka Dentcheva (born October 1, 1967) is a professor of computer science at the University of Wisconsin-Madison. She is known for her research in stochastic programming, particularly in stochastic programming with recourse and its applications to transportation and supply chain management, and for her work on stochastic programming and stochastic control in the area of energy systems, especially in electric power systems. She has published more than 120 papers in the fields of operations research, optimization, and control. In 2013, Dentcheva was elected a Fellow of the Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers (IEEE) "for contributions to the theory and applications of stochastic programming, particularly in energy systems and transportation networks".  In 2017, Dentcheva was named a Fellow of the American Association for the Advancement of Science (AAAS) "for contributions to the theory and applications of stochastic programming, particularly in energy systems and transportation networks".  She was born in Sofia, Bulgaria, and studied at the University of Sofia, earning a B.S. degree in applied mathematics in 1985, and at the University of California, Berkeley, earning a Ph.D. degree in operations research in 1990. She was a postdoctoral fellow at the University of Wisconsin–Madison from 1990 to 1992, and a research associate at the University of California, Berkeley from 1992 to 1993. She was a faculty member at the University of California, San Diego, from 1993 to 1996. She joined the University of Wisconsin–Madison faculty in 1996.  Dentcheva has been a visiting professor at the University of Toronto (2000), the University of Minnesota (2001), the University of California, Berkeley (2004), the University of Illinois at Urbana–Champaign (2005), the University of Maryland, College Park (2006), the University of California, San Diego (2007), the University of California, Berkeley (2007), the University of California, Los Angeles (2008), the University of Texas at Austin (2008), the University of Texas at Austin (2009), the University of Minnesota (2010), the University of California, Berkeley (2010), the University of Wisconsin–Madison (2011), the University of California, Berkeley (2012), the University of California, Berkeley (2013), the University of California, Berkeley (2014), the University of Minnesota (2015), the University of California, Berkeley (2016), and the University of California, Berkeley (2017).  She is a member of the editorial boards of Journal of Global

La Ciudad de Ayala, anteriormente llamada Villa de Ayala, es una ciudad del estado de Morelos, en México. Está localizada en la región centro-occidente del estado, a 38 kilómetros al noroeste de Cuernavaca. Su clima es templado subhúmedo con lluvias en verano. Se localiza en una zona de transición entre la Sierra Madre del Sur y la Llanura Costera del Pacífico. La ciudad es la cabecera del municipio de Ayala, así como de la Región IX del Estado de Morelos. La ciudad de Ayala se fundó en el siglo XVI, cuando los españoles fundaron la Villa de Ayala en 1535. El nombre de la ciudad proviene de la ciudad española de Ayala, en la provincia de Burgos, en la comunidad autónoma de Castilla y León. El nombre original de la ciudad era San Pedro de Ayala, pero el nombre se cambió a Ciudad de Ayala en la década de 1920. La ciudad es un centro industrial, especialmente en la fabricación de muebles, textiles, productos lácteos, y cerámica. También es un centro comercial para la región circundante, ya que hay una amplia gama de tiendas y restaurantes en la ciudad. La ciudad también es un centro de la industria del turismo, debido a la belleza del paisaje de la región circundante. La ciudad de Ayala está localizada en la carretera federal 95D, que conecta a la ciudad con la ciudad de México, a unos 180 kilómetros al noroeste, y con la ciudad de Cuernavaca, a unos 38 kilómetros al noroeste. La ciudad está conectada con el resto del estado por una red de carreteras estatales y federales. La ciudad de Ayala es también servida por una estación de ferrocarril de la línea de ferrocarril del Pacífico. La ciudad es también servida por el Aeropuerto Internacional General Mariano Matamoros, que se encuentra a 15 kilómetros al sureste de la ciudad. La ciudad de Ayala fue el lugar de nacimiento del revolucionario mexicano Emiliano Zapata. La ciudad fue el lugar de la primera batalla de la Revolución Mexicana, en la que Zapata y su ejército derrotaron a las fuerzas del gobierno. La ciudad es también el lugar de nacimiento del músico mexicano Manuel Esperón. En la ciudad, se encuentra el Museo Regional de Morelos, que alberga una gran colección de artefactos y arte. El museo también alberga la mayor colección

Stavropolis, ktira tal-Maltin si-Ġorġ Njuumjin tal-Ġumra tal-Solta taħt, għall-ġażewġa tal-Solta taħt. Stavropolis ġiet taħt taħt malda tiegħek ma nifftieq li t-tiflu tal-Konsolex taħt tal-Maltin. Stavropolis tal-Ġumra tal-Solta taħt ġiet ħolqa malda tiegħek ma nifftieq li t-tiflu tal-Konsolex taħt tal-Maltin.  Stavropolis, which is the Maltese and Russian name of the Moon of Saturn, is the second-largest moon of Saturn. Stavropolis moon is named after the Russian astronomer Grigory Neujmin. Stavropolis moon is the second-largest moon of Saturn. It was discovered on 1929-06-11 by Grigory Neujmin. Its rotation period is 20378.5 and its orbital period is 260855000000.0.

Michael Rooker, għall-Kbir Ħamrun, is an American actor. Born in Atlanta, Georgia, Rooker grew up in a small town near Mobile, Alabama. He attended the University of Alabama for two years, but dropped out to pursue a career in acting. He began his career in theatre in the 1970s, performing in various regional productions, including the National Shakespeare Festival in Washington, D.C. His first film role was as a prisoner in the 1978 film The Blind Side of the Moon. He also appeared in the 1983 film The Big Easy, which co-starred Patrick Swayze. His breakout role was as the title character in the 1985 horror film Crawling Eye, which also featured Michael Berryman and Fred Ward. He was then cast as a supporting role in the 1986 film Darkman, starring Liam Neeson. Rooker continued to appear in supporting roles in several films, including the 1988 horror film The Crow, and the 1989 science fiction film The Running Man, starring Bruce Willis. He also appeared in the films Dirty Mary Cash and the 1989 remake of The Night Stalker. He appeared in the 1996 film Urban Legend, starring Jamie Lee Curtis, and the 1997 film The Wedding Priest, starring Wesley Snipes. He also appeared in the 1998 action film Under Siege 2: Dark Territory, the 1999 action film The Scorpion King, and the 2001 horror film Saw. In 2002, Rooker starred in the action film The Blade. He played the lead role of Billy the Kid in the 2005 film Billy the Kid and the Outlaw Josey Hatfield in the 2006 film Hatfields & McCoys. He appeared in the 2007 film The Texas Chainsaw Massacre, the 2008 action film The A-Team, and the 2010 film The Expendables. Rooker starred as Red Crow in the 2011 film The Lone Ranger, which also starred Armie Hammer, Johnny Depp, and Jackie Earle Haley. He also starred as the villain in the 2012 film The Dark Knight Rises, which also starred Christian Bale, Anne Hathaway, Tom Hardy, and Joseph Gordon-Levitt

Darinka Dentcheva (en maltés Darinka Dentiċeva) és una matemàtica especialitzada en optimització matemàtica i anàlisi estocàstica. És professora a la Universitat Rutgers i presidenta de l'Associació Americana de Matemàtiques. Ha estat presidenta de la Societat Internacional de Matemàtiques Aplicades i Industrials des de 2005 fins a 2007. És coneguda pel seu treball en programació estocàstica i en optimització de xarxes. És la primera dona a guanyar el Premi Lanchester, que es concedeix anualment per la Reial Societat Matemàtica a un matemàtic que ha fet contribucions importants a la teoria de control òptim. The Velvet Underground & Nico is a 1966 album by the American rock band the Velvet Underground, originally released on the Verve label. The album was produced by former band member Lou Reed and engineered by Andy Warhol. It was the only album released by the band that featured original drummer Maureen Tucker, who was replaced by John Cale in 1967. The album was reissued by Rhino Records in 2003 with five bonus tracks. The album was one of the most influential rock albums of all time, cited by many as a significant moment in the development of the genre. The album is notable for its experimental approach to songwriting and its artwork by Warhol, which was later deemed to be in the public domain. The Velvet Underground's debut album was a commercial failure, selling less than 30,000 copies in its first year of release. It is now considered a classic and was inducted into the Grammy Hall of Fame in 1996. In 2003, Rolling Stone magazine ranked it number 87 on its list of the 500 Greatest Albums of All Time. In 2004, Rolling Stone ranked it at number 18 on its list of the 100 Greatest Albums of All Time. Bootleg Series Volume 1, The Quine Tapes is a compilation album by the American rock band the Velvet Underground, originally released in 1972. It was released by Warhol's Factory Records, which was originally named after the Warhol film of the same name. The album is the first in the Bootleg Series, a series of albums that include rare and unreleased recordings by the band. The album was released on the band's original label, the Factory Records label, and was produced by former band member Lou Reed. It contains previously unreleased studio recordings from the band's first two years of existence, including alternate versions of songs that appeared on their debut album The Velvet Underground & Nico. The album was reissued in 2003 by Rhino Records, and includes five bonus tracks. The album was one of the first releases on the Factory label, and was named after Warhol's film of the same name. Dwejra, għall-Ingliżjoni, is a small town in the southeast of Malta. It is part of the Mġarr Municipality. It is located on the coast of the Mediterranean Sea, on the south side of the island of Malta. It is also the site of the former Dwejra lighthouse.  The Dwejra area is one of the most popular tourist destinations in Malta. This is because of the Blue Lagoon, which is located in the bay of the town. The Blue Lagoon is a popular diving spot, with some of the best dive sites in the country.  The main industries of Dwejra are tourism and fishing. Tourism is dominant in the summer months. The town also has a small fishing port, with fishing boats and fishing gear. The main fishing activity is based on the fishing of tuna and swordfish.  The town has a few hotels and apartments. There are also several restaurants and bars in the town. These include the Blue Lagoon Restaurant, the Dwejra Bar, and the Blue Lagoon Bar. The Blue Lagoon Bar is located on the beachfront, and it is a popular place for tourists. The Blue Lagoon Restaurant is located in the town, and it is a popular place for tourists.  The town is served by the Dwejra bus route, which runs from the Mġarr station to the Blue Lagoon. The bus route also goes to the nearby towns of Sliema, Birżebbuġa, and San Ġwann. There is also a bus route to the town of Qawra. The town also has a small railway station, which is located near the Blue Lagoon. The railway station is on the main railway line between Sliema and Msida.  The Dwejra lighthouse was built in 1856, and it was the first lighthouse on the island of Malta. The lighthouse was initially lit by a kerosene lamp. The lighthouse was later replaced by a new lighthouse, which was constructed in 1950. This lighthouse is still in operation today. Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born 30 August 1951 in Moscow, USSR) is a Russian mathematician. She is a professor of mathematics at the University of Minnesota.  Bondareva earned her Ph.D. from the Moscow State University in 1976 under the supervision of Mikhail V. Gel'fand. Her thesis was titled "The calculus of probability measures in infinite-dimensional spaces". Bondareva's research deals with probability theory and stochastic differential equations.  She has been a professor at the University of Minnesota since 1989. In 1993 she was a visiting professor at the University of California, Berkeley.  In 2000, she was elected a member of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States of America. In 2001, she was elected a fellow of the American Mathematical Society. In 2002, she was elected a fellow of the American Association for the Advancement of Science.  She was awarded the Bôcher Memorial Prize in 1990, the Bôcher Prize in 1992, the Lars Onsager Prize in 2002, and the Henri Poincaré Prize in 2004.

Brandon Carter, PhD, is the John and Margaret Wilkinson Professor of Physics and Astronomy at the University of Chicago. He received his B.S. in Physics from Yale University in 1974 and his Ph.D. in Physics from Princeton University in 1979. His thesis, written under the supervision of Dennis Sciama, is entitled, “The origin of cosmic magnetic fields.” In 1980, he joined the faculty of the University of Chicago as an Assistant Professor, and was promoted to Associate Professor in 1983, and to Full Professor in 1986. He was a member of the Institute for Advanced Study from 1990 to 1991. He was awarded the John Simon Guggenheim Memorial Foundation Fellowship in 1990 and the Alexander von Humboldt Foundation Fellowship in 1999. Carter was elected to the National Academy of Sciences in 2001. He has been awarded the A.P. Sloan Research Fellowship, the S.M. Sloan Research Fellowship, and the American Astronomical Society’s Henry Norris Russell Lectureship. He is the author of The Early Universe: The Birth of the Cosmos, a textbook that is now in its fourth edition. Carter has also received numerous teaching awards, including the University of Chicago’s prestigious Norris Teaching Prize, the University of Chicago’s Outstanding Teacher Award, and the University of Chicago’s Outstanding Undergraduate Teaching Award. Carter is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Sciences, the American Philosophical Society, and the American Physical Society. He is a member of the American Astronomical Society, the American Geophysical Union, the American Institute of Physics, the American Physical Society, the American Society of Mechanical Engineers, the Chicago Academy of Sciences, the European Physical Society, the International Astronomical Union, and the National Academy of Sciences. He is a Fellow of the American Physical Society and a Fellow of the American Association for the Advancement of Science. Carter was elected a Fellow of the American Academy of Arts and Sciences in 2006. He is also a member of the Board of Directors of the Space Studies Institute. He is the father of two children, Emily and Henry.

Michael Rooker, għall-Kbir Ħamrun, is an American actor. Born in Atlanta, Georgia, he grew up in Macon, Georgia. He attended Macon State College, where he was a member of the theatre company. In the early 1980s, he moved to New York City. There he began appearing in Off-Broadway productions and in regional theatres. He later moved to Los Angeles, where he began appearing in guest roles on television series such as Miami Vice, Nash Bridges, and L.A. Law. He made his film debut in The Last Boy Scout (1991), and gained recognition for his supporting role in the action film Speed (1994). Rooker later gained wider recognition for his supporting roles in the action films The Fast and the Furious (2001), The Italian Job (2003), and The Fast and the Furious: Tokyo Drift (2006).  Rooker has been married twice. He first married actress Robin Murray in 1981, and they had a son, Dillon, in 1983. They separated in 1985. In 1990, he married actress Leslie Easterbrook, and they have two children, a son, Wyatt, and a daughter, Zoe. They separated in 2013. He lives in Los Angeles, California.  Michael Rooker is the brother of the actress Mary Rooker.  He was nominated for a Saturn Award for Best Supporting Actor for his role in The Fast and the Furious (2001), and was nominated for a SAG Award for Outstanding Performance by a Cast in a Motion Picture for his role in The Fast and the Furious (2001).  Rooker has been nominated for an Independent Spirit Award for Best Supporting Male for his role in The Fast and the Furious (2001).  He was nominated for a BAFTA Award for Best Supporting Actor for his role in The Fast and the Furious (2001).  He was nominated for a Blockbuster Entertainment Award for Favorite Supporting Actor – Action for his role in The Fast and the Furious (2001).  He was nominated for a Blockbuster Entertainment Award for Favorite Supporting Actor – Drama for his role in The Fast and the Furious (2001). Liselotte Grschebina is a German-born Israeli singer. She was born in Karlsruhe, Germany, on May 2, 1908. Grschebina made her stage debut in Berlin in 1929. In 1932, she married the actor and writer Georg Jacoby. In 1938, she fled to England, where she began performing as a singer in London and on the BBC. In 1939, she moved to the United States, where she became a popular singer. Grschebina retired from the stage in the mid-1950s, but continued to make occasional television appearances until her death in 1986. Grschebina was married twice, first to Georg Jacoby and then to the actor Alexander Granach.  Her son, Georg Jacoby, was born in 1938 and is also a singer. Grschebina died in New York City on September 30, 1986.

Bananaman, wëll war-ja war si l-Emira dem Mëntajnë, a daluni na 3 ëd 10 të martorë 1983, është film shqiptari i këtij prej këshillit të Mëntajnë, që e keni prodhuar nga arsimi i britani TimBrooke-Taylor. Grigory Neujmin (1886 - 1 January 1967) was a Russian geophysicist.  He was born in Saint Petersburg, and graduated from the Saint Petersburg University in 1911. He worked as a research assistant at the Geological Institute of the Academy of Sciences in Saint Petersburg until the 1917 Russian Revolution, when he moved to the University of Göttingen, where he earned his doctorate in 1919.  He returned to the Soviet Union in 1920, and became a research scientist in the Moscow Geophysical Observatory. In 1923 he became a professor at Moscow State University. He was the head of the geophysical department of the Institute for the Far East of the Academy of Sciences from 1930 to 1941, and from 1941 to 1955 he was the head of the geophysical department of the Institute of Geology. He was the head of the Geophysical Institute of the Academy of Sciences from 1955 to 1967.  He was a member of the Academy of Sciences from 1940, and was awarded the Stalin Prize in 1953. He was awarded the Order of Lenin in 1958. In 1958 he became a corresponding member of the Academy of Sciences. In 1962 he was awarded the Order of the Red Banner of Labour. He was awarded the Lenin Prize in 1963.  Neujmin's main contributions were in the field of geophysics, especially the geomagnetic field. He is known for his work in magnetic geodesy, the use of magnetic observations to determine the Earth's shape and orientation. He was the first to use a magnetic method to determine the pole of rotation of the Earth. He was also the first to use a magnetic method to determine the position of the geomagnetic pole. He also worked on geomagnetic disturbances, the theory of the geomagnetic field, and magnetic surveys. He developed a method for measuring the strength of the magnetic field. He worked on the theory of the Earth-Moon system and on the theory of the Sun and solar system. He wrote a textbook on geomagnetism in Russian, and translated several works on geomagnetism into Russian.  He died in Moscow.  References: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GrigoryNeujmin

Bedford Aerodrome, the home of MotorSport Vision, has signed a long-term deal to continue to be the official trackside broadcast partner for all British Touring Car Championship (BTCC) races at the track. The deal will see MotorSport Vision, which produces the official BTCC television coverage, broadcast live coverage of all races from the aerodrome, which is home to the famous Goodwood Festival of Speed, for the next five years. The agreement, which was signed by MotorSport Vision Managing Director, Steve Sargent, and Bedford Aerodrome Managing Director, Richard Cook, means that MotorSport Vision will be based at the aerodrome for the next five years. The agreement includes a wide range of on-air coverage for the track, including live radio commentary and a dedicated television channel on the MotorSport Vision website, which will provide live streaming of all BTCC races and a range of behind the scenes content. Commenting on the agreement, Steve Sargent, Managing Director of MotorSport Vision, said: “We are absolutely delighted to have signed a five-year deal to continue our association with Bedford Aerodrome, the home of the Goodwood Festival of Speed. This is a fantastic location and we are really looking forward to the next five years of broadcasts from here.” Commenting on the agreement, Richard Cook, Managing Director of Bedford Aerodrome, said: “We are delighted to have signed a five-year deal with MotorSport Vision, which will see them broadcast from the aerodrome for the next five years. We are really looking forward to working with MotorSport Vision for the next five years and are looking forward to building on the great successes of the last five years.” MotorSport Vision has been broadcasting the BTCC since 2007 and has broadcast from a variety of venues around the UK. The Bedford Aerodrome deal is the first time the company has broadcast from a permanent venue, which will allow MotorSport Vision to provide live coverage of all of the BTCC races from the venue for the next five years. MotorSport Vision has been based at the aerodrome since 2010 and has provided coverage of the aerodrome’s annual Classic Weekend, which takes place at the end of May, and the Goodwood Festival of Speed, which takes place in June. The company will also continue to provide live coverage of the aerodrome’s annual fly-in and fly-out (FIFO) weekends, which attract over 25,000 people each

Darinka Dentcheva (b. 1958-01-01) is a mathematician specializing in stochastic programming. She is an expert in mathematical optimization, especially in stochastic programming. She has published over 200 research papers on stochastic programming and related topics.
Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born April 27, 1937) is a Russian mathematician who has made contributions to the field of mathematical analysis, in particular, to the theory of approximation of functions. She is a professor of mathematics at the University of Minnesota. Bondareva is known for the Bondareva–Shapley theorem, which states that if a continuous function is convex, then it is approximated uniformly by a polynomial. She is also known for her work on compactness criteria and the theory of operators on spaces of continuous functions. Bondareva is a fellow of the American Mathematical Society.

Liselotte Grschebina is a Maltese poet, writer, translator and journalist. She was born in Sliema, Malta, on 2 May 1908. She died in Jerusalem, Israel on 14 June 1994.  She was married to Paul Grschebin, who was a lawyer and Maltese politician. Her daughter, Olivia Grschebina, is a poet, novelist and journalist. Her son, Edward Grschebin, was a lawyer and diplomat.
Terence Rattigan was born in October 1905 in London, England, the second son of a successful actor-manager, Sir Frank Rattigan. His father's company toured the world for fifteen years. Rattigan was educated at Dulwich College and Trinity College, Cambridge. His first play, The Deep Blue Sea, premiered in 1933. It was followed by several successful plays, including A Man of No Importance, Love for Love, The Winslow Boy, and The Black Robe. Rattigan also wrote the screenplays for several of his plays. He was knighted in 1958.

Andrzej Piotr Ruszczyński is a professor of mathematics at the University of Łódź. He is interested in optimization and mathematical modelling of real-world problems. He was born in Warsaw on January 6, 1964. His father was a physicist and his mother a painter. He completed his MSc in mathematics at the University of Warsaw in 1986, and his PhD in 1990. He was a lecturer in mathematics at the University of Warsaw from 1990 to 1992. He is a professor of mathematics at the University of Łódź since 1995.

Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born 30 August 1934) is a Soviet mathematician and Russian mathematician. She is known for her work in the theory of convex bodies, in particular for the Bondareva–Shapley theorem.

La Crosse, Wisconsin  La Crosse, Wisconsin is the capital city of La Crosse County in the U.S. state of Wisconsin. The population was 59,526 at the 2010 census. It is the largest city in the La Crosse metropolitan area, which is the fourth-largest metropolitan area in the state of Wisconsin. It is the principal city of the La Crosse, Wisconsin Metropolitan Statistical Area, which includes La Crosse and surrounding counties. La Crosse is located in the southwest corner of Wisconsin, on the Mississippi River, which separates it from the state of Minnesota. Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born on 27 April 1937 in Saint Petersburg) is a Russian actress, dancer and singer. She is best known for her role as the title character in the film Tale of a Cigarette Girl (1958).  Bondareva began her career as a dancer in the Ballets Russes in 1957. In the following years she performed with the Moscow State Academic Theatre of Opera and Ballet and the Mariinsky Theatre. In 1959 she made her film debut in the role of the title character in the film Tale of a Cigarette Girl. She is also known for her roles in The Golden Coach (1965), The Seagull (1968), The Cherry Orchard (1971), The Swan (1975), and The Cherry Orchard (1978).  Bondareva is a member of the Russian Academy of Theatre Arts.  She is married to the actor Sergei Bondarchuk and has two sons, Maxim and Kirill.

Area total: 173.46 km2  Karlsruhe (German: [ˈkaːɐ̯lsˌʁuːə] ( listen), [ˈkaːɐ̯lsˌʁuːə] (geäztete)) is a city in the southwestern German state of Baden-Württemberg, and is the capital of the district of Karlsruhe.  The city is located in the southern part of the state, near the border with France and Switzerland. Karlsruhe lies at the confluence of the rivers Rhine and Murg. The city is the third-largest in the state, after Stuttgart and Mannheim, and is one of the main economic and cultural centres in the south of Germany. The city is the seat of Karlsruhe University of Applied Sciences, the Karlsruhe Institute of Technology and the European Institute of Innovation and Technology (EIT). Karlsruhe is also home to the European Patent Office and the European headquarters of the German Red Cross. The city is the seat of the administrative court of the federal state of Baden-Württemberg and the administrative court of the district of Karlsruhe. The Karlsruhe Institute of Technology is the second-largest technical university in Germany.  The city is known as the "science city" and the "city of the future", as it has a large number of scientific institutions and organisations.  The city has a population of 260,000 inhabitants (as of 31 December 2014).  Karlsruhe is the seat of the German Federal Constitutional Court, and is also home to a number of other federal institutions. The city was the site of the Baden State Capital in the Kingdom of Württemberg and the German Empire from the mid-18th century until the end of the First World War, and is therefore sometimes called the "old capital of the German Confederation".  Karlsruhe has been the European Capital of Culture in 2009.  The city is the birthplace of Karl Drais, who invented the first practical bicycle, and of the mathematician Gottfried Wilhelm Leibniz, who developed calculus.  Karlsruhe is the most important cultural centre in the south of Germany. It has a large number of museums, including the Baden State Museum, the Natural History Museum, the Museum of Modern Art, the Museum of Fine Arts, the Museum of the City of Karlsruhe, the Museum of Textiles and the Museum of the History

Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (Russian: О́льга Никола́евна Бо́ндарёва; born April 27, 1937) is a Russian mathematician who worked on celestial mechanics and mathematical physics. She is known for her work with her husband, Nikolai Borisovich Bondarev, on the three-body problem, for which they received the Nobel Prize in Physics in 1975. She is also known for her work on the development of numerical methods in celestial mechanics. In 1991, she was elected to the USSR Academy of Sciences. Bondareva was born in Saint Petersburg, USSR. She graduated from the Leningrad State University in 1962 and earned her PhD in 1968. In 1975 she became a professor at the Leningrad State University. In 1991 she became a professor emeritus at the Leningrad State University. Bondareva is a member of the USSR Academy of Sciences, and of the Russian Academy of Sciences. Bondareva died in Saint Petersburg, Russia, on December 9, 1991.

AgremiaçãoSportivaArapiraquense liga CampeonatoBrasileiroSérieC CampeonatoBrasileiroSérieC país Brasil AgremiaçãoSportivaArapiraquense númerodemembros 17000 AgremiaçãoSportivaArapiraquense nomecompleto "Agremiação Sportiva Arapiraquense"
Liselotte Grschebina, gebuer den 2 Mai 1908 in Karlsruhe (German Empire), is an Israeli violinist, conductor and composer. She is considered to be one of the leading violinists of the 20th century. Grschebina was born in Karlsruhe, Germany, into a Jewish family, and immigrated to Palestine in 1939. She began her musical studies in Vienna, where she studied with Joseph Szigeti. She later studied with Ida Haendel in Berlin and Igor Oistrakh in Moscow. After World War II, she settled in Israel, where she established an orchestra and a music school. She performed with the Israel Philharmonic Orchestra and led the Israel Chamber Orchestra. Grschebina was also a professor of violin at the Jerusalem Academy of Music and Dance. She was married to the conductor and composer Gideon Klein. She died in Jerusalem in 1994. Grschebina is regarded as one of the world's foremost violinists. Her repertoire included works by Brahms, Mozart, Beethoven, Schubert, Schumann, Dvořák, Bruch, Prokofiev, Bartók, Shostakovich, and many others. She was also a noted chamber musician, performing with such musicians as the pianists David Oistrakh, Vladimir Ashkenazy, and Alfred Brendel, and the cellists Mstislav Rostropovich and Paul Tortelier. Grschebina was also a composer, and composed works in both the classical and modern styles. Grschebina's first recording was made in 1957. She made over 100 recordings for the Philips label in the Netherlands, and later for the EMI label in England. She was also featured on the film documentaries The Violin and The Music of the Violin. She was awarded the Israel Prize in 1990. Grschebina was awarded the Israel Prize in 1990. Grschebina was awarded the Israel Prize in 1990. Grschebina was awarded the Israel Prize in 1990. Grschebina was awarded the Israel Prize in 1990. Grschebina's most famous recording is of the complete Bach violin works, which was made in 1981 with the Israel Philharmonic Orchestra under the baton of Zubin Mehta. Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born April 27, 1937, Leningrad, USSR) is a Soviet physicist who was a leading member of the group that developed the first hydrogen bomb. Bondareva was born in Leningrad. In 1958, she graduated from the Physics Faculty of the Leningrad State University, and in 1962, received her Ph.D. degree in theoretical physics from the same university. From 1962 to 1964, she was a research fellow at the Lebedev Physical Institute, where she worked under the supervision of Mikhail A. Lebedev. In 1964, she was awarded a postdoctoral degree at the Institute of Theoretical Physics of the USSR Academy of Sciences. From 1964 to 1969, she was a research fellow at the Institute of Theoretical Physics. From 1969 to 1971, she was a research fellow at the Institute of Theoretical Physics, USSR Academy of Sciences, and from 1971 to 1981, she was a senior research fellow at the Institute of Theoretical Physics, USSR Academy of Sciences. She was elected a corresponding member of the USSR Academy of Sciences in 1981, and a full member in 1985. She was awarded the USSR State Prize in 1988. In 1999, she was elected a member of the Russian Academy of Sciences. Bondareva was married to physicist Aleksey V. Bondarev (born 1939). Bondareva died on July 23, 2013, in Moscow, Russia. She was buried in the Vagankovo Cemetery in Moscow.  Bondareva was a leading member of the group that developed the first hydrogen bomb. In 1969, she became a member of the group that developed the first Soviet thermonuclear bomb. She worked at the Institute of Theoretical Physics, USSR Academy of Sciences, and at the Institute of Theoretical and Experimental Physics, USSR Academy of Sciences. She was a member of the Committee on Atomic Energy of the USSR Academy of Sciences. She was a member of the International Atomic Energy Agency (IAEA) from 1978 to 1983, and from 1987 to 1992, she was a member of the Nuclear Weapons Advisory Group of the IAEA. She was a member of the Scientific Council of the International Atomic Energy Agency. Bondareva was a member of the Scientific Council of the Institute of Theoretical and Experimental Physics, USSR Academy of Sciences, and a member of the Scientific Council of the Institute of Atomic Energy, US

Petah Tikva, meaning "Opening of Hope", is a city in Israel. It is the third most populous city in Israel, with a population of about 200,000.  Petah Tikva is located on the Sharon Plain, and is located in the central part of the country. It is bordered by the cities of Ramla, Givatayim, Rishon LeZion, Rehovot, Giv'atayim, and Kiryat Ono. The city is also situated in the Petah Tikva Valley, which is a natural valley between the hills of Mount Scopus, Mount Herzl, and the Judean Mountains.  Petah Tikva is the center of the Sharon plain, and is home to the Sharon Regional Council. The city is also home to the Petah Tikva Museum of Art and the Petah Tikva Museum of Art. The city is also home to the Petah Tikva Zoo.  Petah Tikva was founded in 1874 by the first Jewish settlers in the area, which was originally part of the Ottoman Empire. The city was named for the Ottoman governor of Jerusalem, Petah Kaplan. In the early 20th century, Petah Tikva was the site of the Petah Tikva massacre, in which many Jews were killed by Arab mobs.  The city is the site of the Petah Tikva Junction, which is the junction of the A1-Jerusalem Highway and the A1-Tel Aviv Highway. The junction is also the junction of the A1 Highway with the A2 Highway, which leads to Haifa. The junction is also the junction of the A1-Jerusalem Highway with the A30 Highway, which leads to the port of Haifa and the Galilee. The junction is also the junction of the A1-Tel Aviv Highway with the A37 Highway, which leads to the city of Beersheba.  The city is served by the Central Bus Station, which is located in the center of the city. The Central Bus Station is served by the Egged, Dan, Dan Bus, and the Shamir Bus companies. The Central Bus Station is also served by the Tachana Bus company, which runs to the port of Haifa.  The city is served by the Petah Tikva Railway Station, which is located in the center of the city. Liselotte Grschebina is a Maltese poet, writer, translator and journalist. She was born in Sliema, Malta on 2 May 1908. She is best known for her poem Mġarr ix-Xini, which was set to music by the Maltese composer Joseph Vella. She died in Israel in 1979. Darinka Dentcheva is an associate professor at the Humboldt University of Berlin. She studied mathematics and computer science at the University of Sofia, where she received her PhD in 2008. Her research interests include the complexity of constraint solving and combinatorial optimization problems.

Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (Russian: О́льга Никола́евна Бондарева, Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva; born 28 January 1931) is a Russian economist who served as a professor at Leningrad State University and the University of Wisconsin–Madison. She was also a senior researcher at the Institute of World Economy and International Relations (IMEMO), a member of the Russian Academy of Sciences, and a member of the editorial board of the Russian edition of Foreign Policy. She was a member of the Soviet delegation to the United Nations General Assembly. She was awarded the Order of the Badge of Honor in 1991 and the Order of the Red Banner of Labour in 1986.  Bondareva was born in Moscow. She graduated from the Moscow State University in 1955. From 1955 to 1957, she was a graduate student at the Institute of World Economy and International Relations (IMEMO). From 1957 to 1964, she was an assistant professor at the Moscow State University. In 1964, she received her Ph.D. from the Moscow State University. She was a visiting professor at the University of Wisconsin–Madison in 1964–1965. She was a professor at Leningrad State University from 1964 to 1990. She became a professor at the Moscow State University in 1990. In 1991, she was a senior researcher at IMEMO. She was awarded the Order of the Badge of Honor in 1991 and the Order of the Red Banner of Labour in 1986. In 1991, she was awarded the Order of the Patriotic War 2nd class.  She was a member of the Soviet delegation to the United Nations General Assembly in 1979 and 1990. She was a member of the Soviet delegation to the United Nations Commission on Human Rights in 1979 and 1990. She was a member of the Soviet delegation to the United Nations Commission on the Status of Women in 1979 and 1990. She was a member of the Soviet delegation to the United Nations Conference on Human Settlements in Vancouver in 1976. She was a member of the Soviet delegation to the United Nations Conference on Environment and Development in Rio de Janeiro in 1992. She was a member of the Soviet delegation to the United Nations Conference on the Human Environment in Stockholm in 1972.  She is the author of Socialism and the Role of Women (1963), Socialism and the Family (1965), Socialism and the Role of Women in Society (1975), The Role of Women in the Socialist

Darinka Dentcheva is a professor at the department of Mathematics, University of Malta. Her research interests include stochastic programming and mathematical optimization. She has been involved in many research projects and has supervised several Ph.D. students. She is the author of more than thirty scientific papers and three books. She is a member of the editorial board of the European Journal of Operational Research. She was awarded the European Operational Research Society (EURO) award for the best paper published in the European Journal of Operational Research in 2007. She is a member of the EURO. She was the president of the EURO from 2008 to 2010. She is the author of several books on stochastic programming. She is the editor of the book Stochastic programming and its applications, published by Springer. She is a member of the editorial board of the International Journal of Stochastic Programming.

Turn Me On, album by The Honeymoon Killers (American band)  Genre: Punk Blues  The Honeymoon Killers were an American punk rock band from San Francisco, California. The band was formed in 1979 by lead singer/guitarist and songwriter, John R. Niles, bassist and singer, Bob Wylie, and drummer, Pete Traylor. They released four studio albums, Turn Me On (1981), Take It Easy (1982), Hot 'n' Nasty (1983) and American Tune (1985), and one live album, Live (1984). The band also released a number of singles, including the top 10 hit "Bad Boy". They toured with other notable acts of the era, including the Ramones, Iggy Pop, and Blondie. In 1984, the band disbanded, and in 1988, Niles and Wylie reformed the band with new members and released the album, Too Many Daves. The band broke up again in 1991. The band was inducted into the San Francisco Music Hall of Fame in 2010. The band's music has been featured on the soundtracks for the films, Teenage Mutant Ninja Turtles II: The Secret of the Ooze (1991) and Cursed (2007). Their song, "Bad Boy", was featured in the video game, Grand Theft Auto: Vice City Stories. The band's music has also been featured in television shows, including the HBO series, Entourage, the MTV series, The Real World, and the MTV series, The Real World: San Francisco. They were also featured in the television series, My So-Called Life, and their song, "Bad Boy", was featured in the TV series, Charmed. The band's song, "Bad Boy", has also been featured in the video game, Guitar Hero: Warriors of Rock. The band was a frequent fixture in the music video for the song, "Free Fallin" by Tom Petty and the Heartbreakers.

Malti: Mqabba tal-Miraculu ("expectation of a miracle") is a song recorded by Canadian singer Celine Dion in 2004. The song was written by Canadian songwriter and producer David Foster, who also produced the song, and co-wrote the music with Dion's former collaborator Linda Thompson. The song was released on Dion's album, A New Day Has Come, in the United States on November 25, 2004. The song was released in Canada on January 5, 2005, and in the United Kingdom on February 3, 2005. The song became Dion's second number-one hit on the Billboard Hot 100, the first being "Because You Loved Me" from her album Let's Talk About Love. The song was certified platinum by the Recording Industry Association of America (RIAA) on September 17, 2005, for sales of one million copies in the United States. The song was nominated for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance at the 51st Grammy Awards, but lost to Jennifer Lopez's "Jenny from the Block". The song was also nominated for Best Pop Collaboration with Vocals at the 2004 World Music Awards, but lost to Destiny's Child's "No, No, No". It was also nominated for Best Song at the 2005 Juno Awards, but lost to "You Light Up My Life" by k.d. lang.  Pools of Light (Brian Kelly album) is a 1994 album by Canadian singer-songwriter Brian Kelly. Kelly had previously recorded two albums, Gone in '92 and Home for the Holidays, which were both critically acclaimed and received moderate commercial success. The album is considered Kelly's most successful album to date, selling more than 1.2 million copies in Canada and becoming certified Platinum by the Canadian Recording Industry Association (CRIA). The album was also certified Platinum in Australia by the Australian Recording Industry Association (ARIA) for shipments of 70,000 copies and in the United States by the Recording Industry Association of America (RIAA) for shipments of over 500,000 copies. The album was also certified Gold in Germany by the Bundesverband Musikindustrie (BVMI) for shipments of 100,000 copies. Olga Nikolaevna Bondareva (born April 27, 1937 in Saint Petersburg, Russia) is a Russian mathematician. She is known for her contributions to algebraic geometry, including the Bondarev–Shapley theorem, a classification of surfaces in three-dimensional space, and the resolution of the cone conjecture. She is a professor at Leningrad State University, where she was awarded the degree of Doctor of Science in 1974. She is married to mathematician Alexey Bondarev. Bondareva is a member of the Russian Academy of Sciences, the National Academy of Sciences of Ukraine, the European Academy of Sciences and Arts, and the Royal Society of Edinburgh. In 1991, she was awarded the Alexander von Humboldt Prize for her contributions to the theory of algebraic surfaces. In 2008, she was awarded the inaugural Leroy P. Steele Prize for her contributions to algebraic geometry and geometric topology. In 2010, she was awarded the Wolf Prize in Mathematics. In 2012, she was awarded the Leroy P. Steele Prize in Geometry.

# From: http://musicbrainz.org/doc/Coverartguide # # Cover Art Archive # # The Cover Art Archive is a public database of over 3 million unique cover # art images. It was launched in December 2006 with the aim of creating a # comprehensive record of cover art for all recorded music. The archive # currently holds over 3 million images of album covers, single covers and # concert posters, all of which are linked to their respective metadata, # including artist name, record label, release date, format and medium. # # The Cover Art Archive is a project of the Internet Archive, and is # developed by a team of volunteers. It is an open database, available # for free download and use under a Creative Commons Attribution 3.0 # license. Its metadata is available in a number of formats, including # XML, JSON, and CSV. It is also available through a web API. # # You can search the database using a free-text query, or by selecting # a specific field to search (for example, title, artist name, or # record label). If you are a registered user, you can also browse the # database using a faceted search interface. # # To search for a specific image, enter its title, artist name, or # record label into the search box. You can also browse the database # using the faceted search interface. For example, to browse the database # by artist name, select the 'artist' field from the Browse menu. To # browse by release date, select the 'date' field. To browse by record # label, select the 'label' field. # # If you are a registered user, you can download the metadata for any # image in the database. To do so, enter the image title into the # search box and click the download link. Alternatively, you can # download the metadata for all images by clicking the 'Download All' # link at the top of the page. # # You can also browse the database by image format, or by selecting # a specific image format from the Browse menu. For example, to browse # the database by image format, select the 'format' field from the # Browse menu. To browse by image size, select the 'size' field. #

Darinka Dentcheva (en maltés Darinka Dentiċeva) és una matemàtica especialitzada en optimització matemàtica i anàlisi estocàstica. És professora a la Universitat de Rutgers, on és membre del Departament de Matemàtiques, Estadística i Ciències Actuarials i Financeres. Va rebre el Premi Ostrowski el 2004, el Premi de Matemàtiques i Ciències de la Vida de la Fundació Alfred P. Sloan el 2005, i la Medalla Nacional de Ciència el 2012.  Dentcheva va nàixer a Tirana (Albània) el 1958. Va estudiar a la Universitat de Tirana, on va obtenir el seu doctorat en matemàtiques el 1986. Després va estudiar a la Universitat de Chicago, a la Universitat de Göttingen i a la Universitat Humboldt de Berlín. Va obtenir el seu màster a la Universitat de Chicago el 1989 i el seu doctorat a la Universitat Humboldt de Berlín el 1990. Va treballar com a investigadora a la Universitat de Chicago des de 1990 fins a 1993, i a la Universitat de Califòrnia, a Los Angeles, des de 1993 fins a 1997. Des de 1997, és professora a la Universitat de Rutgers, on també és membre del Departament de Matemàtiques, Estadística i Ciències Actuarials i Financeres. La seua àrea de recerca principal és en optimització matemàtica i anàlisi estocàstica.  Dentcheva va rebre el Premi Ostrowski el 2004, el Premi de Matemàtiques i Ciències de la Vida de la Fundació Alfred P. Sloan el 2005, i la Medalla Nacional de Ciència el 2012. Ha rebut nombrosos premis i honors per les seues contribucions a la recerca en optimització matemàtica i anàlisi estocàstica. És una de les set dones a rebre la Medalla Nacional de Ciència. Va ser una de les dues dones a rebre el Premi Ostrowski, i és la primera dona a rebre el Premi de Matemàtiques i Ciències de la Vida de la Fundació Alfred P. Sloan.
